German President

Continues to Issue Emergency Decrees 52

Restrictions on Bank Payments Slightly Relaxed

Prohibition of Free Buying and Selling of Foreign Currency

Brüning to Visit Rome Soon

French Ambassador to Germany to Be Replaced

US Economic Aid to Germany Opens Up Another Path

Nothing More Than Seeking a Market for Surplus Agricultural Products

National News Agency, Berlin, 1st: German banks are still unable to return to normal. Today, the President issued a supplementary order to the order of the 28th of last month, adding restrictions on bank transactions and payments, only slightly looser than the previous order. The President also signed an emergency decree to manage foreign currency transactions within the country, forcing foreign banks to no longer withdraw loans from Germany, which is tantamount to prohibiting the export of gold. In addition, it is heard that the President will issue another new order to place all domestic banks under government supervision, so that the financial panic can be overcome as soon as possible. The current domestic opinion is more optimistic than in the previous weeks. The general sentiment believes that the current government is sufficient to control the situation and safely overcome the difficulties. It is also expected that since restrictions on bank payments are still in place, the unusual discount rate of the Deutsche Bank can also be appropriately reduced within ten days.

Reuters, Berlin, 2nd: President Hindenburg has approved the ordinance on the trading of foreign currencies, which will take effect on August 4th. From then on, only the Deutsche Bank will have the right to directly buy and sell foreign currencies. All applications to purchase foreign currencies, except for paying interest or repaying the principal of long-term loans, will not be approved.

National News Agency, Berlin, 1st: The date for Chancellor Brüning and Foreign Minister Curtius to visit Italy is currently tentatively set for Wednesday of this week, the 3rd. They plan to arrive in Rome on Friday to meet with Mussolini and Foreign Minister Grandi on Friday and Saturday, the 5th and 6th, and plan to visit the Holy See to meet with the Pope before returning to Germany on Sunday. Because of obvious signs of instability in the domestic political situation, the Chancellor must return to the capital on Monday. After the results of the Prussian plebiscite on the dissolution of the parliament are announced, there may be further changes to all government measures.

National News Agency, Paris, 1st: The current French Ambassador to Germany, Mr. Magilly, has repeatedly requested retirement due to old age. It is heard that the French government has internally appointed the current Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs, Mr. Ponsot, to succeed him. It is said that this move has been agreed to by the German government. Mr. Ponsot has worked with Briand for many years and is able to get along well with him. He is a capable diplomat, so he will certainly be competent for the important task of representing France in Germany. Domestic public opinion is also quite supportive.

National News Agency, Berlin, 1st: Regarding the United States assisting Germany in restoring its economic situation, it is heard that President Hoover plans to use two major commodities produced in the United States, cotton and wheat, as long-term loans to Germany. Negotiations are currently underway with representatives of the German government, German business representatives, and import merchants. It is also heard that the amount of this loan is approximately 150 million marks, with an interest rate of 4.5%.

National News Agency, Washington, 1st: US President Hoover today, through the Ambassador to Germany, suggested to the German government that the United States Federal Farm Board could sell wheat and cotton to Germany on the most favorable terms as an economic aid. The German government has not yet responded, but Stone, the head of the Farm Board, has stated that he is willing to sell wheat and cotton purchased by the price stabilization agency to Germany on credit. The US Farm Board had previously purchased large quantities of wheat and cotton to stabilize market prices and is now urgently seeking a market for them.

Bank of England

Increases Issuance of Large Amount of Banknotes 53

Approved by the Treasury

To Meet Market Needs

Reuters, London, 6th: The Treasury yesterday approved the Bank of England to issue £15 million in banknotes, bringing the total amount of banknotes to £27.5 million. This increase was approved for a period of three weeks. This measure is purely a precautionary plan, because the Bank of England, in view of the large demand for gold in the bank, and because public withdrawals of cash have always been higher before and after the August bank holiday, requested an increase in the issuance of banknotes. The Bank of England currently has sufficient deposits to meet ordinary needs, but the planned increase in the issuance of banknotes is not without foresight. Furthermore, the loan arrangements between France, the United States, and the Bank of England are only temporary plans to tide over the difficult period from now until the end of October when Congress reconvenes. Responsible parties hope that by then the government can prove that the budget can be balanced by saving methods.

National News Agency, London, 1st: Today, it was announced simultaneously in London, Paris, and New York that the Bank of France and the US Federal Reserve Bank have agreed to loan £50 million to the Bank of England, to be shared equally by the two banks. This was decided this morning in Paris by the governors of the two banks, and was agreed upon with the New York Federal Reserve Bank via telephone. The British Treasury also announced simultaneously that it had authorized the Bank of England to increase the amount of banknotes issued on credit from £15 million to £27.5 million within three weeks to meet the needs of the financial market in August, because there is no hope of increasing the gold reserves in the bank for the time being. Therefore, the Treasury has authorized an increase in the issuance of banknotes on credit.

Spain Decides to Cancel

Patents Enjoyed by Foreigners 54

Britain, the United States, Germany, and France Most Affected

National News Agency, Madrid, 1st: It is reported that all patent rights previously granted by the Rivera Dictatorship to foreign companies will be canceled as soon as possible, because legal experts in the cabinet have petitioned the government, saying that the Rivera Dictatorship had no right to grant all patents to foreigners. Therefore, patents obtained by foreigners are all invalid. Currently, the foreign countries that enjoy patent rights in Spain, such as oil, telephone, navigation, and aviation, will be most affected by the cancellation of patents. The patents of Germany and France are limited to commercial aviation. It is said that after the Spanish government cancels all foreign patent rights, it will inevitably hire a large number of foreign experts to promote all industries and commerce. Currently, public opinion in the country strongly supports the abolition of foreign patents, but there are objections to the hiring of foreign experts, especially from conservative newspapers, because it will harm Spain's reputation in the international community.

Important News

Northeast Army 59

Joint Air and Artillery Operations 60

Shi's Army Dares Not Enter Qingfengdian

Northeast Air Force Achieves Repeated Meritorious Deeds

Yu Xuezhong Says Shi Can Only Flee Eastward

Major Battle Expected Between Wangdu and Qingfengdian

Baoding Correspondence: Shi Yousan's troops of the Pinghan Railway, after being lured by the Northeast Army, entered Shijiazhuang on the 21st. The Northeast Army then retreated step by step, and Shi's troops also advanced gradually. Although Shi's vanguard has crossed Xinle and reached Qingfengdian, Shi's troops, in addition to suffering heavy blows from the air force, have also realized that the Northeast Army's strength in the Wangdu area is formidable and dare not challenge them. Therefore, since the 26th, aerial reconnaissance by the air force has revealed that, apart from about a regiment of Zhang Xuecheng's infantry found in Qingfengdian, there are no traces of Shi's troops. Aerial reconnaissance on the 27th revealed that Shi's troops have dug a trench about five li deep eastward from Qingfengdian. At the eastern end of the trench are four or five villages, and wing-like battlements have been dug around the villages to prevent flank attacks. It seems that they have switched to a defensive posture. In addition, Shi's troops have built a deep trench about thirty to forty li long as their last line of defense from Shijiazhuang to Wuji and Shenze. However, the main force of Shi's troops is nowhere to be found. Around 11 PM on the 26th, more than 400 plainclothes agents appeared in the Qingfengdian area at Shi's front line, conducting harassing operations towards the northeast of Wangdu. The Northeast Army dispatched machine gun teams to sweep them, and simultaneously bombarded them with mortars. Within minutes, they were completely defeated. Previously, the Northeast Army dug trenches thirty-odd li southeastward from the Wangdu railway station, and about seven li westward to the mountain peak. Each trench had two lines, the front trench being eight chi deep and one zhang wide, and the second trench being four chi deep and five chi wide, with communication trenches connecting to the rear. All armies were prepared, with Li Zhentang's troops on the right flank, Du Jiwu in the front, and Chen Guanqun's and Dong Yingbin's brigades distributed on the left flank east of the railway. The cavalry brigade under Bai Fengxiang supported the front and right flanks. The 7th Artillery Brigade was distributed in artillery positions on all fronts. The cavalry of the 2nd Army of the Jinpu Railway has now arrived in Xianxian and Anguo in Hejian Prefecture, connecting with the left flank of the 1st Army of the Pinghan Railway, forming a large fan-shaped solid defense, posing an ambush to Shi's troops. However, in recent days, Shi's troops have not dared to advance lightly on the Pinghan Railway and have switched to a defensive posture. In order to break through Shi's main force as soon as possible, Yu Xuezhong, on the morning of the 27th at about 10 AM, consulted with Zhu Lihan, the Training Director of the Chief Executive's Office dispatched by the Xingying (Provisional Headquarters), Chief of Staff Liu Zhonggan, and Chief of the Staff Office Wen Nianzhong. As a result, starting that day, plainclothes scouts were dispatched to reconnoiter the location of Shi's main force, while aircraft were simultaneously dispatched to assist in reconnaissance. If Shi's troops do not challenge within three days after reconnaissance, the Northeast Army will immediately launch an attack, adopting an emergency pursuit strategy. At that time, Commander Yu will personally go to Fangsheng Bridge to command. When Yu departed, all personnel of the military headquarters, except for a large part remaining in Baoding, were assigned to special trains for mobile operations. Zhu Lihan arrived in Baoding on the 26th, reportedly under the orders of the Deputy Commander, to take on the military liaison mission for the First and Second Armies.

The Northeast Air Force's dispatched task force has been very active in recent days. To avoid bombing, Shi's troops dare not operate during the day. Therefore, the air force task force has changed its strategy. In addition to dispatching planes in different directions for reconnaissance and bombing during the day, they are also conducting night flights. Starting from midnight on the 26th, a French-made 36-hour long-range aircraft was used for the first test flight. The aircraft had lights on both wings and its tail. After taking off from the airport, it circled Baoding city once and then flew south. The aircraft carried four 120-pound incendiary bombs. When it passed the Northeast Army's positions in the Wangdu area, each army burned piles of dry firewood in open spaces to identify them as their own positions. When the aircraft reached Qingfengdian after passing Wangdu, it happened to catch Shi's engineers constructing defensive works with lights. The aircraft dropped three bombs and strafed with machine guns, firing over 700 rounds. All but those killed were scattered. The aircraft then flew south to Shijiazhuang and dropped the remaining two bombs in the city. Flames erupted everywhere. After circling Shijiazhuang several times, it returned to Baoding and landed at about 8 AM on the 27th. Chen Honglu, the commander of the dispatched task force, praised the night air combat as an unprecedented new record in Chinese aviation, with excellent results. Around 11 PM on the night of the 27th, two bomber aircraft were again dispatched, one after the other, to fly to Zhengding and Shijiazhuang to disrupt Shi's rear defenses. The aviation dispatched task force in Baoding, originally attached to the First and Second Air Squadrons, received orders from the Xingying and flew back to Beiping from Baoding in three batches on the morning of the 27th at 5 AM. The first team remained in Baoding, responsible for the Pinghan Railway mission. It is said that the second team will proceed to the Jinpu Railway after arriving in Beiping to cooperate with the Second Army. The air force and artillery have now been ordered to conduct joint air and artillery operations. The method is that each reconnaissance aircraft carries a radio, and the artillery positions are also equipped with radios. The air force reports the location, distance, and direction of the enemy's headquarters and main forces detected in the air to the artillery via radio, and the artillery opens fire for bombardment. The progress of the Northeast Army's tactics in recent years is evident.

On the 27th, Yu Xuezhong told reporters that there have been skirmishes along the Pinghan Railway for days, but no major clashes. Our army's advances and retreats are all in steps. Although there have been some casualties, they are no more than a few people. The front troops in the Wangdu area consist of five brigades, plus one cavalry and one artillery brigade. The Miao Brigade is still in the rear and has not yet arrived. Defensive works have been built in the front. The general attack order will be issued after preparations are complete and the situation of both the enemy and our forces is thoroughly understood. Approximately in a day or two. Shi's troops number no more than 60,000, currently divided into three parts.

Page 9

One part is near Handan, numbering about 10,000. Shi Yousan himself is with a part currently in Shijiazhuang, with Shi himself also there. The troops in the north are more numerous, about 40,000, consisting of the four brigades of Sun Guangqian, Shen Keliang, Fang Qi, and Zhang Xuecheng. Most of them are concentrated in Dingzhou. Sun, being a native of Baoding, is familiar with the geography, so his brigade is at the forefront, expanding to both the left and right. However, the easternmost point only reaches Jin County. West of the town road, there are few of Shi's troops. Their line of defense is T-shaped, with a strong front and a weak rear. If the eastern and western routes carry out a pincer attack, Shi's troops will have no choice but to collapse towards the Linqing and Dezhou area in northern Shandong, and may be reorganized by Chairman Han upon instructions from the central government. There is absolutely no way to go to Shanxi. Further south, there are the Central Army and Liu Guitang's troops, so there is really no refuge other than northern Shandong. Currently, on the Jinpu front, our troops are mostly concentrated in Cangzhou, with a total of four infantry brigades, two cavalry brigades, and two artillery regiments. The cavalry has already bypassed the forward troops, launching a coordinated attack, etc.

Previously, Shi's troops had used Shunde as their main location. From Shunde to Shijiazhuang is only 230 li. Now Shi's troops will use Shijiazhuang as their base camp. Shijiazhuang and Baoding are about 250 li apart. South of Baoding along the railway are Yujiazhuang, Fangsheng Bridge, and Wangdu County. Currently, on the northern section of the Pinghan Railway, trains from Beiping only reach Baoding. Baoding to Wangdu has military communication trains extending to Yangqi outside Wangdu. However, there is only one transportation route, where the main force of the Northeast Army is located. South of Wangdu is Qingfengdian, where there are occasional small skirmishes. This place is about to become a major battlefield. Qingfengdian is feared to be transformed to a bloody place. Further south are Dingzhou, Zhaixidian, and Xinle stations. This section, to Xinle, Zhengding, Hutuo River, Yuanshi, Gaoyi, Dachenzhuang, and Fengcun Bridge south of Shijiazhuang, has been destroyed. Seven spans of the Zhengding Bridge's eighteen spans have been damaged. The Xinle Bridge is even more important. After the cessation of hostilities, restoration will be difficult. Wangdu to Baoding is about ninety-odd li, so in the deep of the night, the sound of artillery can be faintly heard in Baoding city. However, the defenses in this section are very solid, and Shi's troops will hardly cross this Rubicon. (July 28th)

After the Fall of Donggu:

Zhu De Flees to Ruijin Wounded 61

Remaining Red Bandits Gather in Xingguo and Yudu

Troops Continue to Search and Suppress Remaining Bandits Separately

Nanchang Correspondence: When the suppression army besieged Donggu, most of the Red Bandits hid in deep mountains and dense forests, attempting to evade annihilation. The suppression army then set fire to the mountains, causing the Red Bandits to flee in all directions. The left and right wings then took advantage of the momentum and advanced sharply, capturing Donggu. The whereabouts of the bandit leaders Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang are unknown. In recent days, various units have been searching for scattered bandits near Donggu. According to captured bandits and locals, it has been learned that Zhu De was also wounded and fled to Ruijin. The headquarters received many reports on the 29th (yesterday) regarding Zhu's wounded escape: (1) Mao Weishou of the 60th Division reported that Tian Fu carried a stretcher from Donggu on the afternoon of the 26th, with over 300 guards before and after, many carrying pistols. It was later learned that the wounded person was Zhu De. (2) Jiang Dingwen reported that on the 27th (yesterday), over 200 remnants were found in various villages near Sanzhai (the border between Xingguo Gulonggang south and Yudu). According to their statements, they all said that Zhu De was seriously wounded and they no longer wished to follow, so they hid in Sanzhai. (3) The Magistrate of Huichang County reported that Zhu De was indeed seriously wounded and has now fled to the territory of Ruijin County, with over a thousand exhausted bandits, many unarmed. Although the county only has 200 local militia guns, they are holding the strategic points and can block the bandits. However, to eradicate the evil, it is requested to quickly dispatch a large army to pursue and eliminate this menace as soon as possible. From this, it can be known that Zhu's injury is likely credible.

According to front-line news, approximately tens of thousands of Red Bandit remnants fled from Donggu and are now gathered between Yudu and Xingguo. The bandits defeated earlier in Lichuan and Shicheng have gathered in Ruijin. Xiang Ying's band is hiding in Naoziling Mountain, a hundred-odd li from Huichang, at the border of Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Fujian. Therefore, the suppression army is continuing to search and suppress separately. The right-wing divisions are focusing on attacking Xingguo, which should be captured during the day. The central and left-wing armies are using one part to search for scattered bandits in the mountains of Donggu, and another part to pursue and suppress bandits in Ruijin and Yudu, in order to clear the remnants of the Red Bandits as soon as possible. Furthermore, according to aircraft reports, most of the bandits in Ruijin have moved west from Jiubao, attempting to connect with the bandits in Yudu and then flee to Huichang to move towards the Jiangxi-Guangdong-Fujian border. However, the Red Bandits are currently breaking into smaller units. In recent days, Luo Zhuoying's troops encountered over a thousand men from the 9th Division of the 3rd Puppet Army in Yuexi, defeating them and seizing over 200 guns and a bundle of puppet Workers' and Peasants' Bank notes, which were immediately burned. Zhu Shaoliang's troops searched for over 500 Red Bandits in the Fangshan Xiaoyuan area, and found over 600 guns buried in the mountains of Eshan and Jiushan. Zhao Guantao's division encountered over 700 scattered bandits in Shirenling and captured them all, executing dozens of the ringleaders with the most heinous crimes and sending the rest to the rear for disposal. Sun Lianzhong, Cai Tingkai, and other units encountered small groups of two to four hundred Red Bandits in Nantuan, Tongluowei, and other places, eliminating them all. Therefore, it is expected that the remaining Red Bandits can be cleared up soon. (July 30th)

An Investigation into the Korean Incident (Continued) 62

The Details of Tragedies in Other Areas: The anti-Chinese riots by Koreans this time have swept through the three Hans (Korea), but the most severe tragedies occurred in Pyongyang, Incheon, Gyeongseong (Seoul), Wonsan, and Busan. The next most severe were in places such as Zhennampo, Sinuiju, Hamhung, Haeju, and Seocheon. The riot in Wonsan began at 7 PM on July 5th. Koreans rang the fire department's alarm bells as a signal, gathering in one place and attacking Chinese barber shops, food stalls, and restaurants. One group of Koreans smashed doors, windows, and equipment, while another group sought out Chinese to beat. Although Japanese police were stationed throughout the streets, they did not stop the attacks. Chinese who were beaten fled to the consulate, where they were taken in by the consulate and the Chamber of Commerce. By the morning of the 6th, over 2,000 people had been taken in. At noon on the 6th, Koreans planned to surround and attack the consulate to beat the Chinese, but fortunately, the consulate requested the Japanese police station to send a large contingent of police to provide strict protection, thus averting danger. By the evening of the 8th, over a hundred Chinese shops had been ransacked and over seventy vegetable gardens had been destroyed. The Chinese were sheltered until the 11th, when they left the consulate. The local Chamber of Commerce prepared funds to negotiate transport to Gyeongseong at half price, and then transferred to Incheon to return to China. The riot in Zhennampo began at 8 PM on July 6th, starting from the western end of the Korean street. Over a thousand Koreans first attacked a Chinese barber shop. As more people gathered, they attacked other streets, breaking into Chinese shops and ransacking them. Those who found Chinese were beaten by the crowd, injuring over a dozen people. It was reported that Chinese vegetable gardens outside the street were also attacked by Koreans, who set fire to houses and caused the Chinese to flee in all directions. Japanese police transported the Chinese in cars to the consulate for temporary refuge. By the morning of the 7th, there were already over a thousand refugees. By the morning of the 8th, five larger Chinese businesses and over a hundred restaurants and food stalls had been smashed. Among them, 30% lost all their goods, and 70% suffered partial losses. The Chinese residents gathered in the consulate began to leave on the 11th to return to their home countries. Those who could not immediately leave were forced to resume business by Japanese police on July 22nd, so only about twenty businesses are currently open. The riot in Sinuiju began on the evening of July 7th. Although there were many Chinese residents in the area, it was separated from Andong by a river. Before the Korean riot on the evening of the 7th, some people who had prior knowledge crossed to Andong, while others sought refuge in the consulate. The Japanese police station, due to its location on the border between the two countries, was unwilling to overemphasize its shortcomings, so its protection was relatively strong. Only a few doors and windows of over a hundred shops in the city were smashed, resulting in little loss. The riot ended at noon on the 8th. The riot was most intense on the island in the center of the Yalu River, where over twenty Chinese food stalls and restaurants were completely destroyed. Yu Fu, a clerk at the Fushengquan food stall, also 42 years old, died from a head injury caused by a large stone. About fourteen people were injured. In addition, riots occurred in Yushan and Beizhen within Sinuiju on the evening of the 7th at 10 PM, with seven shops being smashed and ten people injured. In Yudong, a riot occurred at 6 PM on the evening of the 7th, injuring twenty-eight people and destroying eleven vegetable gardens. The riot in Seocheon occurred at 10 AM on the 4th, smashing six large shops and injuring five people. The riot in Jeongju occurred at 10 PM on the 6th, smashing five shops and injuring over twenty people. The riot in Namsi occurred at 7 PM on the 6th, smashing eight large businesses and seven vegetable gardens. The riot in Susi occurred at 2 AM on the morning of the 7th, injuring seven people and smashing ten shops. The riot in Guseong occurred at 6 PM on the afternoon of the 7th, injuring three people and smashing four shops. The riot in Bocheon occurred at 7 AM on the 6th, destroying eleven vegetable gardens, smashing six shops, and injuring fourteen people. Riots also occurred in Nyungbyun, Uiju Ganggye, Jaseong, Heecheon, Hamhung, and Haeju, with similar patterns. However, this only applies to the Pyongan North and South provinces, Hwanghae Province, Gyeonggi Province, Gangwon Province, and Daeseongjin. As for the Hamgyong North and South provinces and other provinces (Korea has a total of eight provinces), no details have been obtained. In short, there is no place in Korea without traces of Chinese residents. The exact number of people and population is unknown, and the number of deaths, injuries, and damages is also only an estimate. The above riots were most damaging to shops in Korean streets, and less so in Japanese streets. In every Korean city, due to the natural tendencies of the ethnic groups, there are distinct Korean and Japanese residential areas that do not mix. In this Korean riot, Chinese businesses near Japanese businesses were protected by the Japanese businesses. The Koreans feared harming the Japanese (killing a rat near a vase), so they were somewhat preserved, otherwise, they would have inevitably been completely destroyed.

An Overview of the Losses: The losses of Chinese businesses in various places can be divided into direct and indirect losses. Direct losses are those caused by the immediate smashing, while indirect losses are those caused by the closure of businesses after the riot. For direct losses, only Incheon has obtained figures, while other places have not yet started. For indirect losses, there are no statistics for any place. Based on the situation, the direct losses in Pyongyang were heavier than in any other place. Over ten large businesses, with capital of 200,000 (Japanese yen), were completely destroyed. Their debts cannot be recovered due to the destruction of the account books. Although the Japanese side ordered local Chinese businesses to reconcile accounts with debtors, cunning debtors either did not acknowledge the debts at all, or acknowledged only a small amount, claiming that the Chinese businesses had lost their evidence. Therefore, the direct losses of these ten-odd large businesses in Pyongyang are already around three million yuan. Including the 300-odd small businesses and 60-odd vegetable gardens, the losses are estimated to be over five million. Indirect losses are not yet included. In other places, direct losses are lighter than indirect losses. The losses in Incheon are estimated to be around 400,000. The direct and indirect losses in Gyeongseong, Sinuiju, and Zhennampo are estimated to be around 500,000 each. The losses in Wonsan and Busan are estimated to be around 300,000 each. According to last year's survey, there are over 300,000 Chinese residents in Korea. Calculated per person, the direct and indirect losses are estimated to be over 20 million. Among them, merchants account for 60%, farmers (vegetable growers) account for 30%, and laborers account for 10%. After this attack, the savings of Chinese residents accumulated over many years have been almost completely lost. Those who were fortunate enough not to be destroyed, or whose destruction was lighter, will also find it difficult to sustain due to the sluggish business.

The numbers and names of those in Zhennampo and Sinuiju have not yet been compiled. The tables are as follows:

The Future Crisis of Overseas Chinese: The history of overseas Chinese in Korea dates back hundreds of years. The peak was when Korea was subservient to the former Qing Dynasty. After the Sino-Japanese War, as Japanese power expanded, overseas Chinese, unaccustomed to the bullying of the Japanese and Koreans, gradually left. In recent years, many laborers have found it easy to make a living there, and the wages were several times higher than in China, so more have gone there. Engaging in business and growing vegetables are mostly those who have resided there for many years, while laborers come and go every year. Therefore, they can be broadly divided into permanent residents and short-term residents. Among the overseas Chinese, those from Shandong account for 95 percent, while those from Guangdong and the three northeastern provinces account for 5 percent. Among the overseas Chinese from Shandong, those from the Shandong Peninsula, such as Fushan, Wenyi, and Laiyang counties, are particularly numerous. The reasons for this are: first, the distance between Shandong's Zhifu and Incheon, Korea, is only across a strait, which can be reached by boat in one day and night; second, the people of the Shandong Peninsula are known for their strength and seafaring skills, and they regard living abroad as a common occurrence, and they are also more diligent and hardworking, so they have found a unique way of life overseas. In major ports such as Beijing (Seoul), Pyongyang, Incheon, and Wonsan, many Chinese businessmen have worked hard to accumulate wealth and regard Korea as their second home. As Japan manages Korea, it will not tolerate snoring beside its bed. The reason why overseas Chinese have been able to gain a foothold and share a piece of the pie is due to several special strengths: (1) Vegetable cultivation is the unique skill of the people of Shandong. Radishes, cabbages, turnips, and winter mushrooms, all herbaceous horticulture, Shandong overseas Chinese can handle with ease. Growing melons yields melons. When Japanese and Koreans do it, they are either infertile or withered. To this end, the Japanese government has tried to promote research, but in the end, it cannot compare to our experienced gardeners, so they have to allow us to live there. (2) Chinese cuisine is delicious and has a wide variety. Beijing cuisine is especially favored by Japanese and Koreans. Chinese restaurants are located in various ports. The large restaurants in Beijing, such as Penglaige, Sihailou, Daguan Garden, and Yaxulou, are elegant and clean, and the dishes are exquisite. Japanese and Koreans eat there in the hundreds every day. "Zhaba Cai Liang Zhang Pi" (stir-fried meat and bean jelly) is especially favored by Japanese and Koreans, so in the four major ports of Beijing, Incheon, Busan, there are more than a hundred large and small restaurants, and life is quite prosperous. In order to satisfy their appetites, the Japanese and Koreans have to allow overseas Chinese to gain a foothold there. (3) Shandong pancakes and steamed buns are fragrant, sweet, easy to chew, and filling, and are favored by laborers. In general, overseas Chinese account for most of the food shops in Korea. The plaques of Chinese steamed buns are placed in bustling city centers. This is the same as restaurants, and the Japanese and Koreans cannot eliminate them. (4) Chinese people are hardworking and able to endure hardship. In business, credit comes first. Banks in Korea are more willing to lend funds to fake Chinese than to fake Japanese and Koreans. Chinese people tend to pay back the principal quickly when they have a surplus, and there are never any cases of defaulting on debts. This has a deep relationship with local profit-making institutions and is maintained by ordinary banks, which do not want the government to exclude them. At the same time, Chinese shops are convenient to support and sell goods cheaply. For the same goods, Japanese merchants sell for one yuan, Korean merchants sell for ninety cents, and Chinese merchants sell for only seventy or eighty cents. Therefore, Koreans purchase most of their daily necessities from Chinese merchants, so Chinese merchants in Korea have the function of regulating the level of life and stabilizing prices, and are relied upon by the majority of Koreans. Deeply rooted.

One of the shops destroyed in Zhennampo 66

It is difficult to eradicate. However, since this riot, the timid have returned to China one after another, and although the brave still remain, they are also actively cleaning up everything in preparation for returning to China. Before the riot, there were about 300,000 overseas Chinese in Korea, but according to current statistics, there are less than 50,000. Those who have gone in the past cannot live in peace and engage in business, and those who will come in the future are frightened by this incident and dare not go again. And because the Japanese and Koreans jointly boycott Chinese merchants, do not buy Chinese merchants' goods, and do not use Chinese workers. The Chinese cuisine that they used to like to eat is said to be poisoned by Chinese people for revenge, so all industries have plummeted. Although some have resumed business now, I am afraid it will be difficult to last.

Inadequacy of Consular Personnel: The location of our diplomatic officials stationed in Korea: (1) There is a consulate general in Beijing (Seoul), with one consul general, one deputy consul general, two consuls, one assistant consul and one chief clerk; (2) There is a consulate in Sinuiju, with one consul, one deputy consul and one chief clerk each; (3) There is a vice consulate in Wonsan, with one vice consul and one chief clerk; (4) In Busan

Two of the shops destroyed in Zhennampo 67

There is a consulate with one consul, one deputy consul and one chief clerk; (5) There is a vice consulate in Zhennampo, with one vice consul and one clerk; (6) There is an office of the consulate general in Incheon, with one director and one clerk each. Consuls in various places are not affiliated with each other, and each seeks their own way in case of trouble. Among them, there are some who are proficient in Japanese and understand the situation in Japan and Korea, but there are also many who are not very familiar with the language. Before the incident, the Beijing Daily published news about Wanbaoshan, stimulating the Koreans, and on July 2nd and 3rd, the Korean Daily News issued extra editions indiscriminately. Zhang Weicheng, the consul general stationed in Beijing, turned a blind eye and did not protest to the Japanese side to request the cessation of the news, and was also indifferent to the safety of overseas Chinese. After the incident, he was forced by the Beijing General Chamber of Commerce to protest to the Japanese Governor-General's Office. After the incident subsided, he has not yet investigated the number of losses and casualties. What makes the overseas Chinese most dissatisfied is that he seized功劳without labor, bragging about himself in domestic newspapers, how he protested, how he negotiated. Zhang was ordered by the ministry in June of this year to be transferred to the ministry to take up a position, and Lu Chunfang, who succeeded him as the consul general in India, has been late in arriving in Korea. The general overseas Chinese recognize that their own safety is at stake, but Consul General Zhang is mindful of his short-term post and does not care about it. Even if he has not tried to negotiate, even if he negotiates, the Japanese side may not pay attention. However, the principle of diplomatic officials is that they must do their best. Not only that, but Li Zhonggang, the chief clerk of the Consulate General, usually set up his own business and was incompatible with Zhang Weicheng Jida (deputy consul), often scolding him in public. On July 5th, at the time of the Beijing Riot, more than 4,000 overseas Chinese took refuge in the Consulate General. Li gave a speech in public, saying that Zhang Weicheng had betrayed the country, and led a group of ignorant overseas Chinese to take up arms to beat Zhang Ji and others. After the Chamber of Commerce people persuaded them in every way, they stopped. This incident occurred under the protection of a large number of Japanese police, which was extremely shameful to the country. Therefore, the knowledgeable overseas Chinese regard it as a great pain. Pyongyang belongs to the consular jurisdiction of Zhennampo. On the evening of the 4th, local businessmen heard the news and reported it to the Zhennampo Consulate by telephone. Vice Consul Xu Yuanda said that the 5th was a Sunday and he could not handle the matter, and promised to go to Pyongyang on the 6th. On the 6th, the second tragedy began. Xu arrived in Pyongyang from Zhennampo, and was warned by the Japanese that Pyongyang was dangerous. Xu did not get out of the car, but hastily returned in the original car. It was not until July 8th, after Pyongyang suffered its third catastrophe, that he came. At that time, the chaotic situation in the streets had not yet been cleaned up, and the bodies of the overseas Chinese who had died tragically were still lying across the streets unburied. If Xu were bold enough to walk around for a week, he would have at least obtained some evidence that could be used for future negotiations. But Xu was as timid as a mouse, and only went to the shelter and the hospital for a look before returning to Zhennampo in a hurry. He did not pay attention to how to negotiate or how to deal with the aftermath. This is what all the overseas Chinese in Korea hate the most, and they believe that Xu alone was responsible for the Koreans being able to commit violence three times. Among the general consuls, those who are more responsible are Zhu Fu of Sinuiju and Jiang Wencheng of Incheon, who are willing to negotiate before and after the event, regardless of difficulties. It is thanks to this that the overseas Chinese were able to preserve some of their property. Gong Heting, chairman of the Beijing General Chamber of Commerce, Zhou Jingen, chairman of the North Gang Chamber of Commerce, Fu Weigong, chairman of the Incheon Chamber of Commerce, standing committee member Wang Baozhen, and staff and members of the Beijing Party Department risked their lives to rescue the overseas Chinese, resisted the Japanese authorities, and after the event, they rescued the distressed overseas Chinese and sent them back to China. Their enthusiasm and perseverance were admired by the general public. The staff of the Pyongyang Chamber of Commerce were like a plate of loose sand, and Chairman Meng Xianshi was also muddleheaded. If Gong Heting and Fu Weigong were in Pyongyang, they could have reduced some of the damage. In the future, the government may not want Chinese to reside in Korea, but if it does, it must strengthen the consular defenses, and also guide or select general chamber of commerce officials, so that they can help each other in the event of trouble. As for the expenses of the various consulates, they have been in arrears for several months, so that the general foreign officials are hungry and must serve the public. On the day of the event, even if they wanted to send a telegram, they had no money to do so. The consulate buildings, only the one in Sinuiju is barely acceptable, and the rest are mostly dilapidated and dilapidated. The foreign affairs office is related to the face of the country. If it is not repaired like this, how can it prevent people from despising it? The buildings of the Consulate General in Beijing are spacious and served as the residence of the Qing Dynasty's Minister to Korea. Today, dozens of rear buildings have collapsed. Climbing to the rooftop garden of the nearby Mitsukoshi, looking down, one cannot help but feel emotional.

Another Batch of Refugees from Korea 68

Seeking Refuge in Andong 69

Coming from Gangwon Province and other places

Andong Communication: More than 3,000 disaster-stricken compatriots from Korea who had taken refuge in Andong were previously accommodated here and have been successively dispersed in the past few days, and the refugee shelter has been effectively closed. Unexpectedly, the Chamber of Commerce received a telegram from the Chinese Chambers of Commerce in Pyongyang and Wonsan on the morning of the 26th, saying that there were more than 400 disaster-stricken compatriots who would soon go to Andong. Upon hearing the news, the Public Security Bureau immediately sent people to wait at the station. At 8:00 PM on the 26th, 43 refugees from Pyongyang arrived, and at 7:00 AM on the 27th, another 426 refugees from Wonsan fled here. The local authorities immediately sent personnel to compile the numbers according to their names and led them to rest in the former No. 1 refugee shelter, Dan Gui Stage, and provided food and protection as before. The donations from all walks of life totaled more than 16,000 yuan, and there is still more than 4,000 yuan left after deducting the expenses, so it is still sufficient to meet the needs. Zhang Hanwei, the director of the Commercial Port Public Security Bureau, went to the refugee shelter twice on the afternoon of the 27th to express his condolences to the refugees and inquired in detail about the situation when they were in distress in Korea. According to the refugees, they were all laborers who used to work as road repairmen, hawkers, and vegetable growers in the Gangwon Province area. In this change, although the disaster in Gangwon Province was relatively light, the actual damage and losses suffered were also huge. No less than 20 or 30 Chinese people in remote areas were beaten to death by thugs. Unfortunately, there were fewer overseas Chinese there, and the Chinese people rarely pay attention to it, so the country is probably still unaware of these dead compatriots. They also said that after being driven out of Gangwon Province, they took the opportunity to flee to Wonsan for refuge. They were given food by the local Chinese Chamber of Commerce, so they were able to survive. They originally planned to return to their old places after the four borders were slightly calmed down. Unexpectedly, they recently heard rumors that the Korean people were preparing to start another incident on the 30th to expel them. Hearing the news, they were even more shocked, so they decided to return to their country. Fortunately, the two Chambers of Commerce in Wonsan and Pyongyang provided them with travel expenses, so they were able to escape to Andong. According to this, the situation in Korea is indeed not completely settled. Most of these refugees are from Hebei and Shandong. Soon, they will either move to other ports to find work or return to their hometowns. The authorities have prepared travel expenses and will properly distribute them. (28th)

News 2

Ding Chungao and Nan Guixin 70

Process of being arrested one after another 71

Both were noticed by detectives at the train station

They were released after various parties interceded

Tianjin Communication: After Shi Yousan's mutiny, the Northeast authorities paid close attention to the actions of politicians and military personnel in the opposition, in order to prevent them from starting a political storm and making the overall situation even more chaotic. Ding Chungao has the closest relationship with Feng Yuxiang. In the past, he repeatedly served as Feng's representative to contact various parties. In 1928, Ding served as a member of the Hebei Provincial Government. Last year, when Feng failed, Ding resigned. He often traveled between Beijing and Tianjin. As the situation in the north became tense, Ding's actions were noticed by the authorities. Last week, Ding went from Tianjin to Beijing. Plainclothes detectives followed him. When the car arrived at the Qianmendong Station, the detectives called the police and arrested him together with the military police. However, since the Northeast and Northwest are currently promoting unity, he was released the next day after various parties interceded by letters and telegrams. Nan Guixin, the first mayor of Tianjin Special City, has some origins with Yan Xishan. Yesterday morning (27th), Nan and his two sons and two servants arrived in Tianjin by Train No. 202. Nan has been retired for several years. During this turbulent time in the north, his sudden arrival was also noticed by the detectives. After Nan got off the train, he visited old friends of the Jin faction everywhere. The detectives became even more suspicious. In the afternoon at 4:00 PM, Mr. Nan and his sons and servants went to the Dong Station again and boarded Train No. 10 to Beijing. The detectives then reported to the 10th Squadron of the Military Police, and the squadron sent plainclothes military police Li Jingxing and Guan Yuxiu to board the train and arrest Nan at 4:20 PM. He was handed over to the 10th Squadron's general station branch, where Chief Wang Linshu interrogated him. Mr. Nan confessed that he was currently serving as a consultant to the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force (and produced a letter of appointment from Commander-in-Chief Chiang as proof). He said that he had been summoned to Beijing by Mr. Zhang Puquan, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee. Wang knew that it was a mistaken arrest, but he did not dare to release him, and urgently telegraphed to the Deputy Commander-in-Chief of the Military Police in Beiping for instructions. The reply telegraphed ordered him to be sent to the Tianjin Garrison Command for disposal. At 5:30 PM, he was sent to the Garrison Command, which urgently telegraphed to the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force's Executive Office for instructions. Then, Zhu Guangmu, the Director of the General Affairs Office, telegraphed Zhang Ji for inquiries. Zhang replied that he had indeed telegraphed Mr. Nan to come to Beijing and guaranteed that Mr. Nan had nothing to do with the current situation in the north. The Deputy Commander-in-Chief then telegraphed back to order his immediate release. At 8:30 PM, Mr. Nan regained his freedom. The Garrison Command, fearing that he would be arrested again by detectives on the way, specially sent Liu Baohe, the Chief of Investigation of the First District Public Security Bureau, to escort him, and he boarded Train No. 4 to Beijing at 9:00 PM. (July 28th)

Jiujiang Huangdi Embankment Collapses 72

All circles decide to establish a relief committee

Nanshan Road will temporarily resume passenger cars first

Jiujiang Communication: The Huangdi Embankment in Jiangbei, Jiujiang, is a barrier to prevent flooding in the 9th District of the county and Susong in Anhui, Huangmei in Hubei, and Guangji. Recently, the river water has risen sharply. The last line of defense of the embankment, Panxing圩, collapsed for more than 40 feet at Yangjiatang at 1:00 AM on the 1st of this month. The river water was more than 3 feet higher than the fields in the 圩, and it poured straight down like a waterfall. Countless people and animals were drowned. More than 54,000 acres of farmland belonging to Jiujiang were flooded. The loss of rice, cotton, soybeans and other property is estimated at 500,000 yuan. At 1:00 PM on the 1st, all circles here held an emergency meeting and decided to establish a Jiujiang Flood Relief Committee on the 2nd. The Chamber of Commerce will advance 2,000 yuan to handle emergency relief. Refugee shelters will be set up in the three places of Doutian Temple, Dongyue Temple, and Nengren Temple, and a temporary cattle mortgage office will be set up to raise the cattle brought out by the victims. In the future, they will be allowed to pay the borrowed money and take back the original cattle. Because unscrupulous merchants are manipulating the value, a cow worth 70 or 80 yuan can only be sold for 15 or 16 yuan.

The Nanshan Railway was suspended from traffic on the 27th of last month due to the damage caused to the roadbed and bridges by the water. According to the railway bureau's investigation, the water depth on the track from Jiujiang Station to 3 miles and 40 chain的地方 is more than 1 foot, the water depth from 25 miles and 20 chain to 60 chain is more than 2 feet, the道台 at 29 miles collapsed more than 60 feet, and the bridges at 42, 58, 61, 82 and 83 and other numbers were either damaged by the water or submerged by the water, and the situation was very dangerous. In particular, near Yongxiu Station, more than 30 feet of the roadbed earthwork was washed away by the water, and the sleepers and tracks were overturned by the water. The Railway Bureau has ordered workers to rush to repair the road, and it will take at least 5 days to fully resume traffic. In order to facilitate passengers, the bureau has resumed passenger trains from Jiujiang to Nanshan on the 1st of this month. The trains will run once a day at 9:00 AM in sections. Those departing from Jiujiang Station will only go to Yongxiu. There is a springboard at Yongxiu to Tujiapu, a small station 35 miles away. Passengers must walk past, and then change cars at Jianjiapu and drive to Nanchang. The same applies to those departing from Nanchang. Each passenger is only allowed to bring four pieces of luggage, otherwise the railway bureau will not be responsible for overloading. In addition, the Jiujiang Electric Light Company has been out of power since the 27th of last month due to the submergence of the machinery, and it has not yet been restored. (2nd)

Anhui Provincial Government Decides to Re-establish Relief Committee 73

Various Counties Continue to Telegraph Disaster Conditions Daily

Anqing Correspondence: The magnitude of the flood disaster in Anhui Province is unprecedented in decades. More than 40 counties have telegraphed the province to report the disaster. Therefore, at the regular meeting of the Provincial Government on July 31st, the Department of Civil Affairs proposed to re-establish the Provincial Relief Committee as before due to the severe flood disaster in the province. After deliberation, it was decided to adopt the proposal. It is said that the committee will be restored soon. The Provincial Government has received telegrams from various counties reporting the disaster for several consecutive days, roughly as follows: (1) The Xuancheng Emergency Flood Relief Committee telegraphed on the 30th, stating that only the First Jinbao Embankment in Xuancheng remains. It was breached recently, causing great disorder. They urgently request assistance to maintain the current situation. (2) The Langxi Construction Bureau and other groups telegraphed on the 26th, stating that the flood disaster in the county is extremely severe, the worst in 60 years. Six zhang of the city wall have collapsed, the county office is two chi deep in water, the river has overflowed the embankment, and all the crops have been submerged. The bureau and other groups are distributing bread, building reed sheds, and rescuing the people, but it is a drop in the bucket and difficult to cover everyone. They earnestly request that the authorities promptly send relief for emergency distribution to save the lives of all the people. (3) Jiang Shuxun, the Magistrate of Xuyi County, telegraphed on the 29th, stating that after continuous heavy rain, mountain torrents erupted. All four townships of Xuyi County have become a watery expanse, with fields and houses submerged and countless elderly and children dead or injured. Such a catastrophe is too tragic to describe. Local representatives have been selected to go to Beijing and the province to request emergency relief. Furthermore, bandit activity has disrupted transportation in remote areas. It is extremely difficult to collect the second installment of land tax in advance. With no income, it is impossible to maintain the current situation. They specifically request that the allocation of military expenses from the county be temporarily suspended. (4) The Hefei County Party Headquarters and others telegraphed on the 30th, stating that Hefei is unfortunately afflicted by a sudden mountain torrent. The county seat has completely become a watery expanse. All the embankments have been breached, and fields, houses, and dwellings have been washed away. The death toll of people and livestock in urban and rural areas is especially difficult to count. This catastrophic disaster is rarely seen in a century. In addition to the establishment of a flood relief committee by various groups to actively seek relief, they earnestly request sympathy for the disaster victims and a grant of relief, as well as exemption from land tax to alleviate the calamity. (5) Zhou Chongyi, the Magistrate of Quanjiao County, telegraphed on the 27th, stating that after days of heavy rain, the mountain torrents erupted again, and the water level rose several chi higher than before. The severity of the disaster is beyond description. The entire county government is submerged in water, and many houses have collapsed. In addition to borrowing the Chamber of Commerce as an office location and further investigating and reporting on the disaster, they first telegraphed the report. (6) Chen Jiting, the Magistrate of Su County, telegraphed on the 26th, stating that since the beginning of summer, the county has suffered hailstorms and now a flood disaster. The crops have been completely destroyed, and houses, livestock, and people have been washed away. Thousands of refugees have been displaced and are starving. They earnestly request approval to allocate emergency relief and send personnel to investigate and save the people. (7) Luo Wei, the Magistrate of Fengyang County, telegraphed on the 26th, stating that the Huai River embankment in the county has completely breached, with tens of thousands of disaster victims displaced. Please allocate a large sum for emergency relief. (8) The Susong County Party Headquarters and others telegraphed on the 27th, stating that after ten days of continuous rain in Susong, the rice crops in bud have been completely washed away. More than 20 villages in the southeast are trapped by the river tide on the outside and by the accumulated water on the inside. The people's embankments have breached, creating a vast expanse of water. It is still necessary to urgently protect the river embankment to save lives. It is still raining heavily, and mountain torrents are overflowing, causing houses to collapse and creating a scene of widespread misery. Please provide emergency relief to save the people. (August 2nd)

Zhejiang Army Captures Bandit Stronghold in Eastern Jiangxi 74

Zou Qi's Band Almost Completely Annihilated

More Than Sixty Bandit Wives Executed

Nanchang Correspondence: Zou Qi's band of accumulated bandits in eastern Jiangxi (a part of Fang Zhimin's forces), with over a thousand men and about a thousand rifles, have been roaming the Xinjiang and Raohe River basins for years, causing extraordinary disasters in Yiheng and other places. They have now been defeated by Tang Enbo's brigade of the Zhejiang Army, with over 800 bandits killed and 400 to 500 rifles captured. Tang telegraphed news of the victory on the 29th. The original text reads: "Zou, Hu, and other bandit bands sneaked back to the south bank of the river from Huangshagang on [date], and joined forces with Wu Zhiying's band, numbering 1,500 to 1,600 men with about 800 rifles, gathering in the Yangcun area. I immediately dispatched Guiqi and Hekou's Sun and Yu battalions, who rushed to attack at night, and also ordered the Hu militia to encircle and suppress Yangcun from Zixi. When they arrived at Yangcun, it was already late at night, and the bandits were sound asleep. My troops stormed into the bandit stronghold, killing over a hundred men with broadswords. The bandits, awakened in surprise, abandoned their equipment and fled in panic. At dawn the next day, they launched a counterattack against us. At this time, my Hu militia had also arrived, launching an attack from both the front and rear. After more than five hours of fierce fighting, the bandits began to scatter. Over 800 bandits were killed on the spot, and over 400 rifles, over 50 Mauser rifles, and over 10 horses were seized. In addition, over 60 wives of Zou, Hu, and other key bandit leaders were captured and executed on the spot. Countless other stolen goods were seized. Troops are currently being dispatched to conduct a thorough search in the vicinity of Yangcun to clear out the remaining bandits." (July 30th)

Local Correspondence

Jinshan 75

The Tragic Case of Filicide in Zhujing is Judged. Wang Diqing of Zhujing, at the instigation of his mother, Wang Tao, ordered the male servant Xia Aqing and the female servant Xiao Mama to strangle Wang Diqing to death on the night of the fifth day of the fifth lunar month. After Liu Cheng, the judge of Jinshan County Government, began investigating on June 21, he suspected Wang Tao and others. According to public opinion, Wang Tao had an adulterous relationship with the accountant Wang Yutian, which was discovered by Diqing, leading to several conflicts. Wang Tao also restricted Diqing's spending. Therefore, the county government investigated along this line of inquiry. Although Wang Yutian fled upon hearing the news, Xiao Mama confessed first after six investigations, stating that she acted on the orders of her mistress, Wang Tao. That evening at 7:00 PM, Xia Aqing strangled Diqing with a rope around his neck to make it look like a suicide. After the facts of the case were fully revealed, Wang Tao and Xia Aqing knew that denial was useless and confessed. Subsequently, a public debate was held on July 18, with hundreds of spectators crowding the venue. Recently, Judge Liu Cheng, accompanied by Secretary Shen, went to the court to announce the verdict. All the defendants stood solemnly before the court. Judge Liu Cheng read the main text, stating that Wang Tao and Xia Aqing were sentenced to death for premeditated murder, and Xiao Mama was sentenced to 12 years of imprisonment. After hearing the verdict, Wang Tao and Xia Aqing looked pale, drooping their heads in disappointment. Xiao Mama knelt and begged for a lighter sentence, tears streaming down her face. The court was then adjourned, and the defendants were ordered to be returned to custody. The tragic case of filicide that shocked the region came to an end.

Memorial Service for Zhu Zuozhou, Who Died Defending Against Bandits. When the town of Tong'an Bridge in the Suzhou countryside was looted by lake bandits last December, Zhu Zuozhou, the drill instructor of the town's merchant corps, died defending against the bandits. Each department of the merchant corps sent teams to participate. Several hundred representatives from various organizations attended.

Reorganization of the Grain Supplement and Land Classification Office. The Grain Supplement and Land Classification Office under the Wuxian County Land Tax Clearance Committee has already opened. Now, with the change of heads of the finance bureau and the county magistrate, after the new Wuxian county magistrate takes office in the next few days, he will work with the finance bureau to reorganize the office.

Bloodshed in an Opium Den. At around 8:00 PM on [date], Wang Kuaiyuan, Li Zhong, Wang Changsheng, Lu Xiaodi, Yang Weijin, and others went to Xu Shaoqing's opium den at No. 7 Saijin Lane in Suzhou City to smoke opium. They argued with Xu Shaoqing over unpaid debts. Xu Shaoqing suddenly drew a sharp blade and stabbed wildly, also stabbing himself in the arm and head. At the time, Wang Kuaiyuan and the other four were stabbed, with Wang Kuaiyuan being the most seriously injured, suffering four wounds to his abdomen, head, legs, and shoulders. Fortunately, the assailant Xu Shaoqing was immediately restrained and handed over to the police district. Yesterday (August 2nd), he was transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The injured Wang Kuaiyuan and the other four were sent to Guangmin Hospital for treatment that night. Wang Kuaiyuan's life is feared to be in danger.

Wuxi 77

A Sugar Mill Worker Electrocuted. Kuang Apei, a worker at the Li Shunxing Sugar Mill in Zhangcheng Lane, Beitang, Wuxi, was from Jiangyin and 22 years old. The year before last, he came to Wuxi with his wife, Liu, to make a living together. Liu is currently working as a servant at the Wu Dachang Sugar Mill in Mian Lane, outside the West Gate. The afternoon before last, Apei intended to visit his wife during a break from work. However, just as he passed the entrance of Guangshun Depot nearby, a power line snapped and fell to the ground. Upon seeing this, Apei immediately reached out to remove the power line, resulting in electrocution and instant death. Afterwards, the neighbors notified the owner of the Li Shunxing Sugar Mill, who informed his wife, Liu. Yesterday (August 2nd), the local head, together with the deceased's wife, Liu, reported the incident to the county court and requested an autopsy.

Autopsy of a Silk Shop Clerk Who Died Suddenly. After Zhang Wanzheng, a clerk at the Yongsheng Silk and Satin Company at the entrance of Taiping Lane, Tongyun Road, Wuxi, suddenly died, on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at 3:00 PM, Du, an inspector from the prosecutor's office of the county court, led coroner Shen to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy continued until 7:00 PM without conclusive results. Yesterday (August 2nd) morning at 9:30 AM, Inspector Du led coroner Shen, bailiffs, and others to conduct a second autopsy. Coroner Shen washed the body with sorghum wine and conducted a detailed examination, but found no injuries. Then, he inserted a poison detection needle and was able to detect toxic substances, confirming that the death was caused by poisoning. The autopsy was completed at noon. However, the type of poison Zhang Wanzheng ingested could not be determined. Inspector Du ordered the family to prepare a coffin and collect the body. He brought the deceased's mother, Zhang Kong, the deceased's brother, Zhang Jingqing, the deceased's cousin, Qian Yao, as well as Chen Baoshu, the representative of Yongsheng Company, and apprentice Yao Shuren, to the court for questioning. They were ordered to return and await further investigation after the poison has been chemically analyzed.

Nantong 79

Bandit Uprising at the Junction of Tong and Ru. Yu Xian, the leader of the bandits in Tongru, gathered more than 400 bandits and roamed in Jiangzhong Yong'an Sand, southeast of Zhentao. They have been rioting, burning, looting, and killing in the Xuejia Yao Yingfanggang area for days. Village Head Xue and others were brutally killed. The county government dispatched a stationed Pingchao police team on the 1st to join forces with the Rugao police regiment to suppress the bandits.

Increased Slaughter Tax Causes Controversy. The slaughter tax in Tong County has been increased by 10% starting August 1st. Butchers protested and went on strike, petitioning the county government, but without success.

The Wusong Naval Police Department Thoroughly Investigates the Xie Case. Xie Ze, the captain of the 18th Nantong Water Police Unit, was stabbed by his subordinate Yan Zheming. Yan was shot and killed by the police team in front of the court. Due to the complicated circumstances, local circles are advocating a thorough investigation. The Wusong Naval Police Department has dispatched Inspector Chen to Nantong to thoroughly investigate the truth.

Yangzhou 80

Disputes Over Protecting and Opening the Embankment Continue. Recently, many places have suffered from flood disasters, but the areas along the canal and Xiangxia River are particularly dangerous. The water level at Sangu Dike in Jiangdu has reached two zhang two chi one cun. Chushan Dike near Shaobo was opened yesterday (29th). The Jiangdu section of the Lianhe Engineering Office has raised and reinforced the Shahe Dike outside Dongguan to temporarily maintain the current situation. However, in the Gaoyou and Yiying area, the water level is very dangerous, and people are preparing boats for evacuation. The water at the Yumadun in Gaoyou has exceeded the water mark of the opening of the Loba Dike in the Republic of China, making it imperative to open the dike. Therefore, the people of the counties mostly advocate for immediate opening. However, in the Xiangxia River area, the autumn harvest season is approaching. If the dike is opened, the water flowing into the Xiahe River from upstream will not easily flow into the sea, and houses and crops will be destroyed. Therefore, it is advocated to delay the opening. Currently, the two factions of protecting and opening the dike have gathered in Gaoyou and are arguing fiercely.

Danyang 81

Four Bandits Arrested. After the home of Jiang Shuji, a farmer in Suxiang Township, Eastern Township, was robbed by bandits on July 24th, Zou Wusan, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, instructed the detective team to solve the case within a time limit. Now, the detectives Ding Genglong and others discovered the bandits' hiding place and led the police to Dongcun near Lingkou yesterday, arresting two bandits named Jing Lailai and Jing Xiaogou. They also went to Dajingjia Village and arrested Jing, the Second Monk, and Zhou, the Nanyuan Monk. They have all been sent to the county government for interrogation.

Huzhou 82

Villagers Force County Magistrate to Inspect the Flood Disaster. More than a thousand mu of farmland in Suzi, located on the border between the West Gate and Qingdong Gate of the city, had its embankment suddenly collapse at around 7:00 PM on the 29th. As a result, more than 500 farmers gathered with hoes, shovels, rakes, and other tools. At noon today, accompanied by Gao Shenghong, the village head of Suzi Village, they came to the Wuxing County Government to report the disaster. When the county guards saw the people carrying tools, they sounded the alarm and closed the iron gates of the county government, fearing that the situation would escalate. They reported to the county magistrate. After Magistrate Li received the report, the villagers climbed over the walls next to the iron gates, surrounded the county magistrate, and demanded that he immediately go to the village to inspect the situation. Seeing this situation, Magistrate Li, fearing that the villagers would riot, immediately agreed to go. He telegraphed Chen Hongji, the Director of the County Public Security Bureau, to send multiple police officers to accompany him to the village for inspection.

Pinghu 83

The Education Bureau Slightly Levies Watermelon Tax. The watermelon tax in the county was originally under the unified tax bureau, and the annual collection was no less than tens of thousands, most of which was pocketed by the handlers, with less than half being reported. Since the tax bureau was abolished, this tax was not included in the business tax bureau. Chen Hui, the director of the county education bureau, specially obtained approval from the education department to use the watermelon tax as primary school education funds, levying two jiao per dan. Since its implementation, the revenue has been very strong.

The Zhejiang Economic Committee Investigator Arrives in Pinghu. Zhu Jiahui, an investigator from the Provincial Construction Committee's Zhejiang Economic Survey, was recently commissioned to come to Pinghu to investigate the economic situation of Pinghu. All the survey forms in the urban area have been completed, and they have now been sent to the villages.

The Branch Bureau Chief Inspects the Flood Situation. Yao Youmei, the branch bureau chief of the Xindi Public Security Branch Bureau, was ordered by the county government yesterday to go to the villages with Xia Yunfeng, the head of the Third District, to inspect the flood situation. The low-lying fields were flooded, and many ponds were submerged. They could only wade through the water. They have already reported the survey to the county government to plan for the aftermath.

Hangzhou 84

Verdict in the Case of Killing a Mistress. Zhu, the wife of Ma Zhaoming, a native of Dongyang and resident of Chengxin Lane, Tianhanzhou Bridge, Hangzhou City, had an affair with He Jichang, a peddler. Because He failed to borrow money from her, he harbored resentment and lured her to the Jesus Church vegetable garden under the pretext of picking pomegranate flowers for treatment. He stabbed her twice in the abdomen and pushed her into the pond, causing her death. The murderer was brought to the Hangzhou District Court for trial and confessed to the previous events. However, this kind of murder was actually due to the failure of the loan and was committed in a moment of passion, which is different from intentional murder. The court sentenced him to seven years of imprisonment for murder and ordered him to be returned to custody to await execution.

Construction of the Sanmen Bay Motor Road Begins. The first section of the Sanmen Bay Sanyi long-distance motor road in Zhejiang Province has been surveyed and completed, and drawings have been reported for planned construction. It is said that the measured route starts from the wharf along Sanmen Bay, passes through Haiyou Town to Xiaozhumen on Tiantai County, and is 130 li long. The second, third, and fourth sections to Yiwu County, connecting to the Xiaochang Railway lines, are also in progress of surveying.

Ningbo 85

Fire at Twenty Bridge. A fire suddenly broke out at the Xie Xinglong Foreign Goods Store on Twenty Bridge in Ningbo City last night at 9:00 PM. It took an hour to extinguish the fire. It is estimated that two buildings of Xie Xinglong, one building of Ren Shunxiang Rattan Basket Store, and one building of Yile Tian Hotel were burned down. In addition, half of the building of Yuanxiang Fruit Store was demolished. The total loss is estimated at more than 6,000 yuan.

Ningbo Chamber of Commerce's Statement Regarding the Inspection of Ship Passengers. The Ningbo General Chamber of Commerce, regarding the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's forced vaccination of passengers on ships from Ningbo to Shanghai, in conjunction with the National Seaport Quarantine Office, sent a letter to the Shanghai Health Bureau and the National Seaport Quarantine Office yesterday. The letter stated that preventive vaccination is a matter of hygiene and is of course for the health of individuals. However, applying it to ships between Shanghai and Ningbo and forcing it is inappropriate. The port of Wusong is very crowded, and it is difficult to complete the vaccinations by name. This matter was first seen in Ningbo. If it is forced, it will inevitably cause disputes. It will not only hinder the company's business but also increase the hindrance to navigation safety. Moreover, after a detailed investigation by the Chamber of Commerce, there is no epidemic in Ningbo, so there is no need to inject cholera and inspect stool. Please exempt it to maintain the shipping industry.

Supervisory Committee Member Gu Pengcheng Sentenced to Eight Months. Gu Pengcheng, the current standing member of the Supervisory Committee of the Xiangshan County Party Department, was accused by the joint name of the 21 Village Committee of Xiangnan for embezzling public funds and forging accounts. Due to various obstacles, the county government delayed the verdict. Yesterday, the Higher Court instructed that the case be transferred to the Yin County District Court for trial. It is now learned that the court has already rendered a verdict in the case yesterday. The main text is that Gu Pengcheng was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for the crime of embezzling public property. Wei Zuoting and Xie Baoru were each sentenced to three months of imprisonment for the crime of jointly forging evidence in a criminal case related to others.

Anqing 86

A Flood Disaster Across Anhui Province. Various counties in Anhui Province have been experiencing floods in recent weeks, which are exceptionally tragic. The Juji Guangji Dike in Huaining County and the Fenglin Mapu Dike in Wuhu have been breached one after another. The damage to people and livestock is incalculable. Other counties such as Dangtu, Fuyang, He County, Quanjiao, and Guichi are almost entirely flooded, and all the fields and houses are submerged. The magnitude of this flood is unprecedented in decades. The provincial government has allocated funds to provide relief to various counties, including 5,000 yuan for the Guangji Dike emergency repair, 3,000 yuan for Huoshan, 2,000 yuan each for Quanjiao, Shouxian, and Wuwei, and 1,000 yuan each for Fuyang, Huaiyuan, Taihe, Suxian, Haoxian, Wuhe, Qianshan, Huo County, Lujiang, Bengbu, Dingyuan, Chuzhou, Fengtai, and Guichi. Other counties are discussing, and not a single county is not seeking relief. Provincial Chairman Chen Diaoyuan originally planned to go to Jiangxi within a few days, but due to the major disaster throughout the province, he had to stay in Anhui to take charge. Fearing that the Guangji Dike disaster victims would cause trouble in the city, the provincial government has appointed a garrison commander to declare martial law. After 10:00 PM at night, pedestrians are prohibited on the streets. Anqing Wanyi Granary is a large granary storing grain, with a reserve of 20,000 dan of grain. It has now opened a rice mill to provide relief. The price of rice in Wuhu, the provincial capital, has suddenly increased by two yuan per dan.
